Automatic fisher ^nN4x7J0t

Clock Input ^LDORbxjB

Sequencer only cycles once when given a signal. Used for casting process (often done in 4 parts). ^D0UYmEqK

Write Input ^RUScL686

Casting Output #2 ^vAYDSXtz

Casting Output #3 ^AbFKleiL

Casting Output #4 ^rHxY5V4a

Methods to Automatically Cast
- Attachment stasis + Rocket
  1. Rocket Activates
  2. Attachment releases, flinging the arm/rods forward
  3. Attachment connects, returning structure back to original position
  4. Rocket Deactivates
- Spike + Servo
  1. Servo lowers an arm used to cast
  2. Spike attaches to rubber/some block at the end of the arm
  3. Servo goes up, causing stress due to the spike holding the arm in place
  4. Spike releases, quickly shooting the arm to expected position ^dJClH5YC

Casting Output #1 ^rqAu1zmf

Diode without diode ^74DAIo8e

Clock Input ^ZoDpFGas

Generic Output ^lDBUDtJ0

Functions the same as a diode for those who do not have the manifest gamepass. Only sends the signal after 2 clock ticks, potentially causing problems for some use cases. However, this can be used in replacement of diodes for this type of autofisher. ^70wshrJH

Make sure nothing touches! ^VIaYb96p

Rod(s) Input ^RoRCgPJZ

Casting ^yuxZKoDI

Stage ^VhRDR421

Detects if rod(s) are in their reeling or idle state.
- Signal 1 (caught a fish) turns on reeling.
- Signal 2 (fish fully reeled) turns off reeling, initiates casting. ^ZGVCfF86

Clock Input ^821jcsgw

Generic Output  ^LDnp9fnk

Methods to Automatically Reel
- Springs + Tripwire
Once reeling starts, clock inputs will continuously power/unpower a spring or set of springs (2 are often used) to move the rod(s) up and down to simulate movement and reel. Can be upgraded by using an Anti-gravity device, but requires extra gates to make sure it is off when casting.


- Disconnected rotation
After disconnecting the hook/line from the rod base, attaching the rod base to a toggle-able spinner (Archerfish, Leafblower, Rocket, etc.) allows for wireless reeling without putting stress on the rod bases. ^71duxJcs

Only springs should not be used as heavy fish prevent spring movement and thus reeling ^ySNfx1D5

No clock toggle needed, can simply be connected to the rod(s) input ^1uu5uEla

Stager using multiple rods ^9LgYYmMu

Reeling ^i16fRS1c

Clock Input ^jNqnVn2q

. . . ^vjNzUaX2

. . . ^B7eWWlsB

Wireless Gate Output ^NTgJzZB8

Make sure each diode in the back is connected to the output/other connected diodes. ^ol6uYRaE

. . . ^4P5CmBQz

Front ^Mm7RyasQ

Back ^EotkhzzR

Separating each rod input prevents signals from coming in too quickly, a major issue with binary counters
If creating a bulk fisher with many rods, using 2-4 rusty rods for the rod inputs gives similar results (rusty rods are slightly slower than normal rods, often sending a signal after normal rods have something on the line) with much less building to accommodate for each rod. ^g4THXa0g

It is crucial that no unintentional connections are made. Use the edges of each transistor if necessary! ^iHslbKG7

Rod Inputs ^hoDKgAeD
